[![Minimum rustc version](https://img.shields.io/badge/rustc-1.63.0+-lightgray.svg)](#rust-version-requirements)\\n7: //!\\n8: //! # PCAP and PCAPNG parsers\\n9: //!\\n10: //! This crate contains several parsers for PCAP and PCAPNG files.\\n11: //!\\n12: //! Compared to other similar projects, it is designed to offer a complete support of the many\\n13: //! possible formats (legacy pcap, pcapng, little or big-endian, etc.) and features (pcapng files\\n14: //! with multiple sections, interfaces, and endianness) while using only safe code and without\\n15: //! copying data (zero-copy).\\n16: //!\\n17: //! The code is available on [Github](https://github.com/rusticata/pcap-parser)\\n18: //! and is part of the [Rusticata](https://github.com/rusticata) project.\\n19: //!\\n20: //! # The pcap format(s)\\n21: //!\\n22: //! The [PCAP] format (files usually ending with `.pcap` extension) is rather\\n23: //! trivial. The [PCAPNG] format (usually `.pcapng` extension) is much more complex: it\\n24: //! can be composed of multiple sections, each with multiple interfaces, having\\n25: //! different capture lengths, time precision and even endianness!\\n26: //!\\n27: //! These formats are more containers than data formats: packets contain data,\\n28: //! formatted according to its interface linktype. There are *many* possible\\n29: //! linktypes, defined in the [linktypes registry]. Support for parsing some of\\n30: //! them is provided using the `data` feature (disabled by default).\\n31: //!\\n32: //! This crate provides an abstraction over these different formats.\\n33: //!\\n34: //! [PCAP]: https://wiki.wireshark.org/Development/LibpcapFileFormat\\n35: //! [PCAPNG]: https://pcapng.github.io/pcapng/\\n36: //! [linktypes registry]: https://www.tcpdump.org/linktypes.html\\n37: //!\\n38: //! # Parsing a file\\n39: //!\\n40: //! `pcap-parser` provides several ways of parsing pcap data. Choosing the right\\n41: //! one is mostly driven by resources: if the input file is small, the\\n42: //! `parse_pcap` and `parse_pcapng` functions can be used directly.\\n43: //!\\n44: //! Fine-grained functions are also available, to parse specifically some block\\n45: //! types for example. They are listed in the `pcap` and `pcapng` modules.\\n46: //!\\n47: //! If the input is larger and cannot fit into memory, then streaming parsers\\n48: //! are available. They work by iterating on blocks, and so do not require to map\\n49: //! the entire input. They cannot seek to a specific block, however.\\n50: //!\\n51: //! *Note: due to PCAPNG limitations, it is not possible to directly seek in\\n52: //! a file to get a packet and handle it: the caller has to iterate though the\\n53: //! file and store (at least) the interface descriptions for the current\\n54: //! section, in order of appearance.*\\n55: //!\\n56: //! ## Example: streaming parsers\\n57: //!\\n58: //! The following code shows how to parse a file in the pcap-ng format, using a\\n59: //! [`PcapNGReader`] streaming parser.\\n60: //! This reader provides a convenient abstraction over the file format, and takes\\n61: //! care of the endianness.\\n62: //!\\n63: //! ```rust\\n64: //! use pcap_parser::*;\\n65: //! use pcap_parser::traits::PcapReaderIterator;\\n66: //! use std::fs::File;\\n67: //!\\n68: //! # let path = \\\"assets/test001-le.pcapng\\\";\\n69: //! let file = File::open(path).unwrap();\\n70: //! let mut num_blocks = 0;\\n71: //! let mut reader = PcapNGReader::new(65536, file).expect(\\\"PcapNGReader\\\");\\n72: //! loop {\\n73: //!     match reader.next() {\\n74: //!         Ok((offset, _block)) => {\\n75: //!             println!(\\\"got new block\\\");\\n76: //!             num_blocks += 1;\\n77: //!             reader.consume(offset);\\n78: //!         },\\n79: //!         Err(PcapError::Eof) => break,\\n80: //!         Err(PcapError::Incomplete(_)) => {\\n81: //!             reader.refill().unwrap();\\n82: //!         },\\n83: //!         Err(e) => panic!(\\\"error while reading: {:?}\\\", e),\\n84: //!     }\\n85: //! }\\n86: //! println!(\\\"num_blocks: {}\\\", num_blocks);\\n87: //! ```\\n88: //! See [`PcapNGReader`] for a complete example,\\n89: //! including handling of linktype and accessing packet data.\\n90: //!\\n91: //! See also the [`pcapng`] module for more details about the new capture file format.\\n92: //!\\n93: //! For legacy pcap files, use similar code with the\\n94: //! [`LegacyPcapReader`] streaming parser.\\n95: //!\\n96: //! See [pcap-analyzer](https://github.com/rusticata/pcap-analyzer), in particular the\\n97: //! [libpcap-tools](https://github.com/rusticata/pcap-analyzer/tree/master/libpcap-tools) and\\n98: //! [pcap-info](https://github.com/rusticata/pcap-analyzer/tree/master/pcap-info) modules\\n99: //! for more examples.\\n100: //!\\n101: //! ## Example: generic streaming parsing\\n102: //!\\n103: //! To create a pcap reader for input in either PCAP or PCAPNG format, use the\\n104: //! [`create_reader`] function.\\n105: //!\\n106: //! # Serialization\\n107: //!\\n108: //! Support for serialization (*i.e.* generating binary data) is available by\\n109: //! enabling the `serialize` feature.\\n110: //! Most structures gain the `to_vec()` method (provided by the `ToVec` trait).\\n111: //!\\n112: //! Note: support is still experimental, though working. API may change in the\\n113: //! future.\\n114: \\n115: #![deny(/*missing_docs,*/\\n116:         unstable_features,\\n117:         unused_import_braces, unused_qualifications)]\\n118: #![deny(unsafe_code)]\\n119: #![allow(clippy::upper_case_acronyms)]\\n120: // pragmas for doc\\n121: #![deny(rustdoc::broken_intra_doc_links)]\\n122: #![cfg_attr(docsrs, feature(doc_cfg))]\\n123: #![doc(test(\\n124:     no_crate_inject,\\n125:     attr(deny(warnings/*, rust_2018_idioms*/), allow(dead_code, unused_variables))\\n126: ))]\\n127: \\n128: mod utils;\\n129: pub use utils::{Data, MutableData};\\n130: \\n131: mod blocks;\\n132: mod capture;\\n133: mod endianness;\\n134: mod error;\\n135: mod linktype;\\n136: pub use blocks::*;\\n137: pub use capture::*;\\n138: pub use error::*;\\n139: pub use linktype::*;\\n140: \\n141: pub mod pcap;\\n142: pub mod pcapng;\\n143: pub use pcap::*;\\n144: pub use pcapng::*;\\n145: \\n146: pub mod traits;\\n147: \\n148: #[cfg(feature = \\\"serialize\\\")]\\n149: #[cfg_attr(docsrs, doc(cfg(feature = \\\"serialize\\\")))]\\n150: mod serialize;\\n151: #[cfg_attr(docsrs, doc(cfg(feature = \\\"serialize\\\")))]\\n152: #[cfg(feature = \\\"serialize\\\")]\\n153: pub use serialize::ToVec;\\n154: \\n155: #[cfg(feature = \\\"data\\\")]\\n156: #[cfg_attr(docsrs, doc(cfg(feature = \\\"data\\\")))]\\n157: pub mod data;\\n158: \\n159: // re-exports\\n160: pub use nom;\\n161: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/pcap-parser--dibench@7fc73b8e4b0b5a0a54b3caeeec206b69d55b4ec3/-/blob/src/lib.rs\"}"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"7f824038-50cc-4407-a8d1-ea54c4cf27b0","uuid":"c1b73402-4090-4e8e-a021-38fc67486199","tool_use_result":{"content":"{\"content\":\"1: //! [![License: MIT](https://img.shields.io/badge/License-MIT-yellow.svg)](./LICENSE-MIT)\n2: //! [![Apache License 2.0](https://img.shields.io/badge/License-Apache%202.0-blue.svg)](./LICENSE-APACHE)\n3: //! [![Crates.io Version](https://img.shields.io/crates/v/pcap-parser.svg)](https://crates.io/crates/pcap-parser)\n4: //! [![docs.rs](https://docs.rs/pcap-parser/badge.svg)](https://docs.rs/pcap-parser)\n5: //! [![Github CI](https://github.com/rusticata/pcap-parser/workflows/Continuous%20integration/badge.svg)](https://github.com/rusticata/pcap-parser/actions)\n6: //! [![Minimum rustc version](https://img.shields.io/badge/rustc-1.63.0+-lightgray.svg)](#rust-version-requirements)\n7: //!\n8: //! # PCAP and PCAPNG parsers\n9: //!\n10: //! This crate contains several parsers for PCAP and PCAPNG files.\n11: //!\n12: //! Compared to other similar projects, it is designed to offer a complete support of the many\n13: //! possible formats (legacy pcap, pcapng, little or big-endian, etc.) and features (pcapng files\n14: //! with multiple sections, interfaces, and endianness) while using only safe code and without\n15: //! copying data (zero-copy).\n16: //!\n17: //! The code is available on [Github](https://github.com/rusticata/pcap-parser)\n18: //! and is part of the [Rusticata](https://github.com/rusticata) project.\n19: //!\n20: //! # The pcap format(s)\n21: //!\n22: //! The [PCAP] format (files usually ending with `.pcap` extension) is rather\n23: //! trivial. The [PCAPNG] format (usually `.pcapng` extension) is much more complex: it\n24: //! can be composed of multiple sections, each with multiple interfaces, having\n25: //! different capture lengths, time precision and even endianness!\n26: //!\n27: //! These formats are more containers than data formats: packets contain data,\n28: //! formatted according to its interface linktype. There are *many* possible\n29: //! linktypes, defined in the [linktypes registry]. Support for parsing some of\n30: //! them is provided using the `data` feature (disabled by default).\n31: //!\n32: //! This crate provides an abstraction over these different formats.\n33: //!\n34: //! [PCAP]: https://wiki.wireshark.org/Development/LibpcapFileFormat\n35: //! [PCAPNG]: https://pcapng.github.io/pcapng/\n36: //! [linktypes registry]: https://www.tcpdump.org/linktypes.html\n37: //!\n38: //! # Parsing a file\n39: //!\n40: //! `pcap-parser` provides several ways of parsing pcap data. Choosing the right\n41: //! one is mostly driven by resources: if the input file is small, the\n42: //! `parse_pcap` and `parse_pcapng` functions can be used directly.\n43: //!\n44: //! Fine-grained functions are also available, to parse specifically some block\n45: //! types for example. They are listed in the `pcap` and `pcapng` modules.\n46: //!\n47: //! If the input is larger and cannot fit into memory, then streaming parsers\n48: //! are available. They work by iterating on blocks, and so do not require to map\n49: //! the entire input. They cannot seek to a specific block, however.\n50: //!\n51: //! *Note: due to PCAPNG limitations, it is not possible to directly seek in\n52: //! a file to get a packet and handle it: the caller has to iterate though the\n53: //! file and store (at least) the interface descriptions for the current\n54: //! section, in order of appearance.*\n55: //!\n56: //! ## Example: streaming parsers\n57: //!\n58: //! The following code shows how to parse a file in the pcap-ng format, using a\n59: //! [`PcapNGReader`] streaming parser.\n60: //! This reader provides a convenient abstraction over the file format, and takes\n61: //! care of the endianness.\n62: //!\n63: //! ```rust\n64: //! use pcap_parser::*;\n65: //! use pcap_parser::traits::PcapReaderIterator;\n66: //! use std::fs::File;\n67: //!\n68: //! # let path = \"assets/test001-le.pcapng\";\n69: //! let file = File::open(path).unwrap();\n70: //! let mut num_blocks = 0;\n71: //! let mut reader = PcapNGReader::new(65536, file).expect(\"PcapNGReader\");\n72: //! loop {\n73: //!     match reader.next() {\n74: //!         Ok((offset, _block)) => {\n75: //!             println!(\"got new block\");\n76: //!             num_blocks += 1;\n77: //!             reader.consume(offset);\n78: //!         },\n79: //!         Err(PcapError::Eof) => break,\n80: //!         Err(PcapError::Incomplete(_)) => {\n81: //!             reader.refill().unwrap();\n82: //!         },\n83: //!         Err(e) => panic!(\"error while reading: {:?}\", e),\n84: //!     }\n85: //! }\n86: //! println!(\"num_blocks: {}\", num_blocks);\n87: //! ```\n88: //! See [`PcapNGReader`] for a complete example,\n89: //! including handling of linktype and accessing packet data.\n90: //!\n91: //! See also the [`pcapng`] module for more details about the new capture file format.\n92: //!\n93: //! For legacy pcap files, use similar code with the\n94: //! [`LegacyPcapReader`] streaming parser.\n95: //!\n96: //! See [pcap-analyzer](https://github.com/rusticata/pcap-analyzer), in particular the\n97: //! [libpcap-tools](https://github.com/rusticata/pcap-analyzer/tree/master/libpcap-tools) and\n98: //! [pcap-info](https://github.com/rusticata/pcap-analyzer/tree/master/pcap-info) modules\n99: //! for more examples.\n100: //!\n101: //! ## Example: generic streaming parsing\n102: //!\n103: //! To create a pcap reader for input in either PCAP or PCAPNG format, use the\n104: //! [`create_reader`] function.\n105: //!\n106: //! # Serialization\n107: //!\n108: //! Support for serialization (*i.e.* generating binary data) is available by\n109: //! enabling the `serialize` feature.\n110: //! Most structures gain the `to_vec()` method (provided by the `ToVec` trait).\n111: //!\n112: //! Note: support is still experimental, though working. API may change in the\n113: //! future.\n114: \n115: #![deny(/*missing_docs,*/\n116:         unstable_features,\n117:         unused_import_braces, unused_qualifications)]\n118: #![deny(unsafe_code)]\n119: #![allow(clippy::upper_case_acronyms)]\n120: // pragmas for doc\n121: #![deny(rustdoc::broken_intra_doc_links)]\n122: #![cfg_attr(docsrs, feature(doc_cfg))]\n123: #![doc(test(\n124:     no_crate_inject,\n125:     attr(deny(warnings/*, rust_2018_idioms*/), allow(dead_code, unused_variables))\n126: ))]\n127: \n128: mod utils;\n129: pub use utils::{Data, MutableData};\n130: \n131: mod blocks;\n132: mod capture;\n133: mod endianness;\n134: mod error;\n135: mod linktype;\n136: pub use blocks::*;\n137: pub use capture::*;\n138: pub use error::*;\n139: pub use linktype::*;\n140: \n141: pub mod pcap;\n142: pub mod pcapng;\n143: pub use pcap::*;\n144: pub use pcapng::*;\n145: \n146: pub mod traits;\n147: \n148: #[cfg(feature = \"serialize\")]\n149: #[cfg_attr(docsrs, doc(cfg(feature = \"serialize\")))]\n150: mod serialize;\n151: #[cfg_attr(docsrs, doc(cfg(feature = \"serialize\")))]\n152: #[cfg(feature = \"serialize\")]\n153: pub use serialize::ToVec;\n154: \n155: #[cfg(feature = \"data\")]\n156: #[cfg_attr(docsrs, doc(cfg(feature = \"data\")))]\n157: pub mod data;\n158: \n159: // re-exports\n160: pub use nom;\n161: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/pcap-parser--dibench@7fc73b8e4b0b5a0a54b3caeeec206b69d55b4ec3/-/blob/src/lib.rs"}}}

See <https://wiki.wireshark.org/Development/LibpcapFileFormat> for details.\\n4: //!\\n5: //! There are 2 main ways of parsing a PCAP file. The first method is to use\\n6: //! [`parse_pcap`]. This method requires to load the entire\\n7: //! file to memory, and thus may not be good for large files.\\n8: //!\\n9: //! The [`PcapCapture`] implements the\\n10: //! When a SHB is\n27: //! encountered, this means a new section starts (and all information about previous section has to\n28: //! be flushed, like interfaces).\n29: //!\n30: //! ## Endianness\n31: //!\n32: //! The endianness of a block is indicated by the Section Header Block that started the section\n33: //! containing this block.
